## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (mechanical vibrations / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator described by position x and velocity v over time t, which is the standard state-space form of forced/damped nonlinear vibration models. Common relationships express dv_dt as a restoring force in x plus damping in v and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign encoded in c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring plus damping proportional to velocity)
- Constant/external bias force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity offset, actuator bias, constant load)
- Sinusoidal forcing (driven oscillator): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external drive)
- General harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c3 * t) (phase-flexible periodic drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity + damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear spring behavior)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping)
- Rayleigh damping nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear dissipation)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * (1 - c3 * x**2) * v (negative damping at small amplitude, limit cycle)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle oscillations with viscous damping)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear parametric stiffness: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (Duffing + parametric drive)
- State-dependent forcing/coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * cos(c3 * t) (modulated forcing proportional to displacement)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative mechanical oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)), reflecting symmetric potentials.
- Conservative vs dissipative split: terms depending only on x (or sin(c*x)) suggest potential-driven motion; terms proportional to v (or v**3, v*Abs(v)) indicate energy dissipation or injection.
- Hardening/softening identification: presence and sign of an x**3 term in dv_dt indicates Duffing-type stiffness (hardening vs softening depending on coefficient sign).
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: factors like (1 - c*x**2)*v (or similar amplitude-dependent damping) are signatures of van der Pol–type negative damping at small amplitudes and stable oscillation amplitudes.
- Aerodynamic/frictional drag: v*Abs(v) (quadratic) or sign-like velocity dependence is typical when drag scales with speed squared rather than speed.
- Large-angle pendulum behavior: sin(c*x) restoring terms indicate periodic-in-angle mechanics, distinguishing from small-angle linearization dv_dt ~ c*x.
- External periodic drive: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms imply forcing at a drive frequency; multiple harmonics indicate non-sinusoidal periodic forcing.
- Parametric excitation: time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v) such as (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x indicate modulation of stiffness/damping, often leading to resonance bands.

Structure desc      : Additive model with linear x and v, a standalone cosine forcing in t, a v-amplitude-modulated cosine term v·cos(·), a mixed polynomial v·x^2, and a cubic velocity term v^3. Variables: x appears only linearly and within v·x^2; v appears linearly, as the amplitude of a cosine, and in v·x^2 and v^3; t appears inside both cosine arguments. With c5≈0.0205 the v·cos(·) modulation is weak compared to the main linear v term (c1≈-0.435) and the stronger mixed term (c8≈0.467), while c9≈0.00546 makes v^3 a small nonlinearity. Since c3≈1 and c4≈-π/2, c2 cos(t-π/2)≈0.309 sin(t); overall approximately -3.93x -0.435v +0.309 sin(t) +0.0205 v cos(3.84 t-1.25) +0.467(vx^2) +0.00546 v^3.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO9)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
0.3064552763\sin t\;-\;0.4243105872\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x\big(0.06821634757|v|^{1/3}+1\big)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x.
\]
Rewrite key structure:
- Forcing: \(A\sin t\) (pure time sinusoid, no \(x,v\) factor).
- Damping-like polynomial term: \(-0.4243\,v + 0.4243\,v x^2\) (i.e., linear in \(v\) plus \(v x^2\)).
- Nonlinear friction term: \(-K\,x\,|v|^{1/3}\) (fractional power of \(|v|\), multiplied by \(x\)).
- Linear stiffness term: \(-3.8545782186\,x\) (since there are two separate \(-1.9272891093 x\) terms).

So any matching candidate must be able to produce simultaneously:
1) a pure \(\sin t\) (or \(\cos(\cdot)\) phase-shifted) term,
2) both \(v\) and \(v x^2\) terms with linked coefficients (can be independent in candidate; that’s fine),
3) an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (this is the hardest: fractional power \(1/3\) of \(|v|\) times \(x\)),
4) a linear \(x\) term.

Now check candidates.

1. Linear/poly in \(x,v\), cos(t), plus \(v\cos(\cdot)\), \(v x^2\), \(v^3\). **No \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**. Cannot match.
2. Has \(v|v|\) (i.e., \(|v|^2\) with sign), not \(|v|^{1/3}\), and not multiplied by \(x\). **Cannot**.
3. Has \(x\), \(x^3\), \(v\), cos(t), \(v x^2\), and \(x\sin(\cdot)\) (time sinusoid multiplied by \(x\), not pure). **No \(x|v|^{1/3}\)** and forcing form wrong unless set that term 0 and use cos for forcing; still missing fractional term. **Cannot**.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO9)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
-0.424310587218182*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.92728910930903*x*(0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.92728910930903*x + 0.30645527626767*sin(t)
```

Let me expand this:
- `-0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `-1.92728910930903*x*0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.92728910930903*x`
- `-1.92728910930903*x`
- `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Combining:
- `x` terms: `-1.92728910930903*x - 1.92728910930903*x = -3.85457821861806*x`
- `v` term: `-0.424310587218182*v`
- `v*x**2` term: `+0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` term: `-0.131504938*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
- `sin(t)` term: `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

So GT = **A*x + B*v + C*v*x² + D*x*|v|^(1/3) + E*sin(t)**

where A, B, C, D, E are specific constants.

The key basis functions are:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `v` (linear)
3. `v*x²`
4. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` — this is crucial and unusual
5. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + phase)`)

Now let me check each candidate for the presence of `x*|v|^(1/3)` or something equivalent.

**Critical observation:** The term `x*|v|^(1/3)` is a very specific basis function. None of the standard terms like `v**3`, `v*|v|`, `x**3`, `x**5`, `v*cos(...)`, `x*cos(...)`, `cos(cx)*cos(...)`, `x³*|v|`, `v*exp(...)`, etc. can reproduce this term.

Let me check if any candidate contains this basis function or can generate it:

- `x*|v|^(1/3)` requires a fractional power of `|v|` multiplied by `x`.

Looking through all candidates:
- Most have polynomial terms in x, v, combinations like `v*x²`, `x³`, `v³`, `v*|v|`, `x⁵`, etc.
- Some have `cos(c*x)*cos(c*t+c)` which introduces x-dependent oscillation
- Candidate 30 has `x**3*Abs(v)**c9` — this could give `x³*|v|^(1/3)` but NOT `x*|v|^(1/3)`
- No candidate has `x*Abs(v)**c` with a free power on |v|

None of the candidates contain the term `x*|v|^(1/3)`. Since this is a linearly independent basis function (fractional power of |v| times x), it cannot be reproduced by any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in x and v, trigonometric functions, exponentials, etc.).

The coefficient D ≈ -0.1315 is non-zero, so this term cannot be ignored.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify each verdict:

Candidates 1-50: All lack the `x*|v|^(1/3)` basis function, which is essential and has a non-zero coefficient in the GT. By the linear independence principle, none can match.
